Hungary Spirit of nacism and shovinism is still here. The worst airport is by far Franc List 2 in Budapest. When leaving the country, we suffered the worst possible mistreatment and chauvinism, when the employee recognized that we were from Serbia, she waited for my wife to put the things in the container, ran up while the things were moving, and ordered her to take off the new shoes and put them in the new the dish. She said that it was a thick platform and that there could be a bomb there. We were in shock and didn't have time to react. It was good that we didn't react, they already had an arrest ready. My wife ran 60 meters to the other end and I brought her shoes. Three meters away from us was another employee who watched us closely while we were looking for clean socks to wear over the dirty ones so as not to ruin our new shoes. I will mention that it could only fit a smaller box of matches, 4.5cm x 3cm x 1cm, maybe 5 grams of explosives. Of course, the only sin was that we were from Serbia, which the Austro-Hungarian Monarchy attacked in the First World War and killed 28 percent of the entire population, women and children, and 62 percent of that was the male population. When my wife was getting up, an aggressive hand with a belt appeared and pushed me away and closed access to the chair. Then we escaped the second arrest. That second employee was informed by the first that we are from Serbia. We passed through the fenced area, the belt closed behind us. there was only one passenger in front of us who was examined at passport control in 10 seconds. When it was our turn, the officer was checking something for 4 minutes. Since I am extremely tall, he knew that I was from Serbia. After 4 minutes, when he saw what we were doing, that we didn't have any crime, that we weren't criminally prosecuted and so on, he picked up the folded passports and handed them to the counter. I thanked him, and he looked at me with an endless expression of hatred and put the passports down. Then we felt fear. We were only in a large room. I pretended that everything was fine. I looked "disinterestedly" into the transparent glass, looking back I didn't see anyone behind us. After 8 minutes, since we didn't react, he picked up the passports again. There we avoided the third arrest, since we didn't react. We passed and arrived at our gate, where there were only two other passengers. we logged in to the internet, using our names as they ask for at the airport, and we were there for about 10 minutes. Then the system crashed. we tried to log in again. They kept asking us to log in again. At the gate next to ours, everyone was on the Internet without any problems. We realized that they were making fun of us since they turned off our bus after they found our names and that we shouldn't complain otherwise... the moment we got off the gate there were three of us on the bus. Suddenly after 2 minutes, another 67 Hungarians got off. The bus started quickly, arrived at the ATR-72 plane, we quickly got on board in 5 minutes, and in 5 minutes with the safety procedure, quickly left the runway, quickly took off, so as not to be late, while changing the engine three times sound on takeoff and that was it. The stewardess told us that the plane had been waiting on the runway for 40 minutes without any reason and that they didn't understand anything. What we experienced as Serbs, oh chauvinism, was nothing compared to what the Jews who returned to Jerusalem experienced. Namely, they were in the part of the airport 80 meters apart from the other counters in the part for special harassment. There were closed passages, with strong police forces and a police dog. And there was only a big queue. Until 1944, the population of Budapest had about 23 percent Jewish population, during 3 months, 560 thousand Jews were killed under the chain bridge on the Danube, and most of them were taken to the Auschwitz camp, where they were mostly killed within a few days. That is why they return to their holy places every year, and the Hungarians remind them when they leave that they have nothing to look for in Hungary. So. In its roots, Hungary still lives under the spirit of Nazism and chauvinism. 6:09 This is a translation issue. Around 45 000 are "obdachlos" and 650 000 are "wohnungslos". Both "wohnungslos" and "obdachlos" mean homeless in English but only obdachlos means homeless as English speaking people know it, like living on the street. Wohnungslos means "being without your own accomodation". Those people live with friends or family but are not considered in a legal contract of this accomodation. So they can be kicked out by them at any time. That makes them vulnerable and that's why Germany is counting them in statistics. But again, "only" ~45 000 are living on the streets (still a bad number). BTW, I was wohnungslos myself for 8 months when studying because I was moving and couldn't find accomodation around the university that quickly. So I stayed at a friends house. Had a great time there but was still part of the statistics.
I don't think any of us were surprised at the France fact.

I am not up to scratch with Andorrans' smoking habits to be frank, but fwiw Andorra traditionally has always been a travel destination for Spaniards and French smokers seeking to stock up on cheap cigarettes, due to their low tax regime. I wonder if that's whats inflating their smoking statistics, if the source is their tobacco sales volume.   Back in the '80s, many travel agents used to organise weekend coach trips filled to the brim with travellers of all ages trying to smuggle cheap cigarettes, electronics into Spain; gigantic chocolate tablets were very popular too, as well as tinned dutch butter, cheese and more. That's the place you'd travel if you needed a new camera or stereo as well.   It was so busy that it wasn't possible for everyone to get checked by customs. Instead, a few people would be selected for a thorough inspection, whilst for the rest some officers would get on the coaches and do a visual check.   I got 1st and 2nd hand hand tales of innocently looking elderly ladies covering their legs with blankets in an attempt to hide all the tax-free goodies under their seats they'd just bought, including tens of cigarette cartons for the family! üòÇ  Like I said, I have no idea how things are these days. Just thought I'd throw this hypothesis as it makes sense to me.

As an Italian, I found the "fact" of Italy being the least culturally diverse country in Europe to be the least believable of all those mentioned in the video. Italy received lots of immigration in recent years and is way more ethnically diverse than a lot of other European countries (over 10% of the population is made up by immigrants). And even if we were talking about ethnically Italian sub-cultures, Italy is defo one of the most diverse countries in Europe from that point of view. The current Italian territory was still split into many smaller states with different languages and traditions only about 150 years ago, so what the hell are we even talking about? It would be interesting to know who came up with that notion and how they performed their research. Btw even Wikipedia shows that there are lots of of countries with lower linguistic, ethnic, and religious fractionalization than Italy. Looks like RealLifeLore got it wrong this time.
There's a pretty large degree of inconsistency in this video.  1. "Least religious" 2. "Best cig sales" 3. "Most marijuana consumed" 4. "Most beer/hard alcohol consumed."  While the argument can be made that Estonia is the "worst at being religious" that logic doesn't translate to the counties who are technically the "best at smoking/drinking"  Especially when looking at such a medically benign product as marijuana which has far more benefits associated with it than negative side effects (thus why the end of it's prohibition globally has occurred so rapidly, such would not be occuring so quickly if there wasn't such strong scientific data suggesting it is not only non-harmful, but has numerous medicinal properties)

I'm from Croatia and i would add this:  Croatia is the worst at not using its full potential. The amount of potential being wasted is huge, more than other countries. I would say only 30% of Croatian's full potential is being used. Even with 30% we are somehow keeping up, imagine what we could do if we used 100% of the potential. We are so slow at progressing, our government is extremely corrupted and lazy.. We could be one of the richest and most developed countries in Europe, but sadly we are on the poor underdeveloped side.  Tourism - We could be on top of the list if we wanted to, we could beat Spain for example, but we are nowhere near that level because our politicians are happy with low profit, they take enough for themselves and don't care about the rest. We have beautiful lands, beautiful ocean with beautiful beaches, hotels, restaurants, luxury apartments, nightclubs, festivals etc.. We have major historical sites all over the country from different eras and of huge importance, but they're not being marketed enough.  Land usage - A large part of the land with rich soil is not being used, especially in the Slavonija region. We still import a lot of products when we could grow it ourselves. That land is being wasted for nothing. They never fixed it after the war even 30 years later. We have lots of natural resources we could use.  Export - We could become a huge exporter of supplies and resources, if we used our lands to the full potential. But as i said, we still import things from other countries instead of turning the table around, instead of growing and selling, we are wasting and buying. We could produce many typed of foods and other products, great wines and olive oils, but we are only doing it on a small scale and it's expensive for us..  Fishing - With the Adriatic sea, we could become a major exporter of fish and other sea food, but again we are not using it fully. How can Norway become a major supplier in salmon, but we cannot do the same with other fish? We still import fish from other places. I worked in a restaurant where we sold squids from Africa and Asia marketed as Croatian Adriatic squids hahah..  Technology - We have the potential to have great scientists and technology development, to invent and produce for the whole world. But we are not doing anything about it, because we still rely on other countries to develop things that we buy. We could also have programmers to create videogames and other software, but we're not doing it.  Education - We have a great potential to have some of the best schools and universities. We could attract students all over the world to come here for education. But it's all being wasted on useless things.. Our education system is completely outdated and a waste of time..  Entertainment - We have the potential to create great movies, music and other arts. But everything we make is average and mediocre, and it's not being marketed worldwide. For example Serbia is beating us with movies and TV shows, their cinema is on a much higher level. Why can't we do it, i don't understand.. We have great actors, singers, musicians, but they end up as amateurs because they're not using the full potential.  Sports - Some of the best athletes and sports teams come from Croatia, but again they're not being used to the full potential and they don't generate enough profit, they don't push forward and our managers are not interested too much into staying in Croatia.   - Football - We have many great Croatian footballers and a fantastic national team. I won't name them all, but more than 50% of Croatian football players are world-class and they're playing for top-level clubs. If we had a proper organization, our national team would win trophies long time ago. Our football league could be at least on the level of Bundesliga or Ligue 1, but instead our league is like Russian or Asian leagues..  - Handball team is also one of the best, and while handball may not be as popular as football, we could still generate great amounts of profit if we had a proper sports organization.  - Martial arts - I'm sure everyone heard of Mirko Filipoviƒá Cro Cop. But we have other fighters as well, and we could produce some of the best fighters and have a good organization if we wanted to. Too bad USA took our Stipe Mioƒçiƒá haha..  - Other sports (olympics, tennis, basketball etc.) - We are great at that too, we have/had many great athletes like Sandra Perkoviƒá, Blanka Vla≈°iƒá, Janica and Ivica Kosteliƒá, Goran Ivani≈°eviƒá etc. but we are very underrated and not using them to the full potential.  Military - Our military could be very powerful if we didn't allow other countries to interfere in our business. We could create our own weapons instead of buying, and we could sell them to other countries. How can Turkey have their own arsenal? How can Austria produce the Glock and Steyer AUG and sell it all over the world, but we don't market our own weapons such the VHS?  Shipyard - Our shipyard Uljanik in Pula could've been great, we could produce ships for other countries and sell them. But sadly it's bankrupt and now rotting in rust..  Cannabis - We could have legalized marijuana long time ago and create a huge business for the whole country. We could generate profit like Canada, USA, Uruguay, Czech Republic, Spain.. Our tourism would flourish and literally everyone in the country would make profit. Not just from tourism, but that unused land could be used for growing crops. We could produce other products from it both for our people and export. And generally speaking, the whole population would be happier and progressive like Canadians for example.  Currently other countries are earning millions and millions from cannabis, because there are only few countries where it's legal. And eventually cannabis will become legal worldwide and the prices will drop significantly. Instead of Croatia using this situation to take as much profit as possible, they are still hesitating and waiting. Once it becomes legal worldwide it won't be such a huge business, it will be like coffee, salt or rice for example.. But until then, only criminals are taking all the profit for now..  Medicine - We could make medicines for export, both chemically and naturally. We could use that cannabis for medicine as well. But now we import medicinal cannabis from Germany. Many types of medicine is unavailable in our country, and instead of producing our own we buy from other countries. Or it's not allowed to import at all. Smaller and poorer countries like Macedonia, Greece, Bosnia etc. they have more and better medicine available. Our doctors could have been top-level as well, if we invested more in medicine and technology. But now most of the good doctors moved to other countries, and we are left with inexperienced youngsters who are not educated enough to become high level doctors. belgiums statistic is wrong.we didn't have the highest covid mortality rate, or in the very least this was only caused by unequal data being used since we counted excess deaths way more liberally. Going through some datasets we are one of the few countries that has more 'covid deaths' than excess deaths. this means that more deaths were categorised as a covid death than there were actually caused by covid heavily skewing the mortality rate. Especially since a lot of countries did the opposite where they counted excess deaths as non covid even though they should be included in the statistics.  If you look at excess deaths per 100k you will see a more true picture of the impact corona had on countries even though you still can't account for other variables atleast your data is more equal.

In greece, do you know how outdated many systems were compared to for example where I live in the Netherlands? THAT is the main reason for sure. It has nothing to do with the average Greek and their incredible generosity. For example. Im sure that my country the Netherlands is one of the best charity nations on the planet. But the average Dutch citizen is absolutely not warmhearted nor hospitable. Dutch people on average are individualistic, often enough rude or big mouthed, and at best friendly. So, this charity stuff statistic is absolutely meaningless when it comes to how people are doing good deeds for others. It's just not in the charity kind of way in Greece due to no systems/institutions in Greece being good at it or efficient. It's already a pain to pay your electricity bills, let alone do something like Charity. But believe me, Greeks are extremely hospitable, and I have the most amazing stories of a large amount of people giving me presents of all sorts, even when they just came to know me in just 30 minutes or less. And this only scratches the surface. Greece has also a word that doesn't exist in any other language. It's called Philotimo. Search it and google it. That Germany number for homeless (97 out of 10.000, 650.000 total) is BS. First, there are 83.000.000 people in Germany, so 650.000 is more like 78 out of 10.000. OK, still bad. But then, the actual number for homeless is 48.000, which brings us to 5 to 6 out of 10.000. The 650.000 mentioned in the video is the number of people without their own (owned or rented) flat (German "Wohnungslose)! That is people searching for a flat because they are currently crushing with friends and/or family, living in a government or otherwise financed dorm, live in some accommodation for refugees (that alone are 375.000) etc. I guess the German word "Wohnungslose" was wrongly translated to homeless. The German word for homeless is "Obdachlose". Makes you wonder what other "facts" that video got wrong.

Just to clarify, Bulgaria being the poorest country in the European union, is still richer than all of the ones outside of the EU outside of Switzerland, Norway and Turkey. The population decline is more on the mentality side more than anything. More and more people are becoming aware of the reality of the situation, the reason why so many left the country in the 90s and early 2000s is starting to slowly fade. People become more aware that living in a foreign country is giving less and less benefits as time goes on. People have actually started returning. Even more are expect to return. However, there are still a lot of people leaving in hope of finding better realization elsewhere. I even personally have family members who in the early 2000s left the country, to Spain and France, that have now come back to Bulgaria and don't plan on leaving, since reality hits when you start your new life in a foreign country, no friends, you're all alone in a foreign place, and things, as it turns out are not that much easier, so people tend to start returning. That said, for many things have worked out after leaving the country for another, so many will not be coming back. Also another reality is that this is happening to the entirety of Europe, many Europeans are leaving their home country for another, however the reason why most are still on a positive growth is because foreigners from poorer countries from Africa or the Middle-East are actually flocking right now. Which is keeping things together for now. However if you start looking at the birth rates you'll soon come to the realization that things are on the decline as the world modernizes, people start having fewer children. This is why the Population growth is expected to almost halt at about 11 billion in just a hundred years time. Since it is expect that most of the world will be able to modernize at that point and most people will be having like 1-2-3 kids. Which is not a bad thing to be honest. That way the consumption of resources will be just about stabilized as well, so we probably won't run our planet into the ground.

'[Iceland] has the least amount of land that's suitable for agriculture'. Exactly. People always meme about how Iceland is green and Greenland is icy, but most of the 'green' in Iceland isn't grass, it's moss. You see grass in some areas near rivers, waterfalls and populated areas, but when you actually drive around Iceland, the vast majority of the land is either volcanic sand or volcanic rock (which is often covered in moss). It suddenly isn't actually very green once you go there.

I feel like a few of these aren't things that countries are the 'worst' at. It's really just aspects of the culture that are deemed negative by western standard. For example, here in Czechia, drinking beer is a very social activity and is ingrained into daily life, and although we don't have a smoking rate near Andorra's, cigarettes are likewise incorporated into daily life. Neither of these activities are necessarily bad; yes they harm health, but arguably it makes people happy and creates a social environment that is very welcoming. The amount of times I've started an interesting conversation with someone at a bar because I forgot a lighter when going out for a smoke break are innumerable.

I've been to Andorra, and I'll tell you why you are wrong about the smoking statistics. The number you cited isn't how much Andorrans smoke, but how many cigarettes are sold per time unit per capita. Andorra, just like many other tiny countries (San Marino, Lichtenstein, Luxembourg, Monaco...) profits greatly from having much lower taxes on things like cigarettes, alcohol, gasoline etc., because the inhabitants of the neighbor more populous countries (in this case Spain and France) are frequently visiting there and buying these things in bulk. You'd see huge supermarkets in Andorra la Vella full of these products especially for these customers, which probably contribute more revenue than all the inhabitants of Andorra combined.

Belgium has the highest reported death rate due to COVID-19 (I thought Peru was first but these things tend to evolve rapidly), which isn't necessarily the same as the highest death rate and if you look at excess death  Belgium is basically the only country in which this lines up (nearly) perfectly with the reported COVID deaths, Belgium did some unconventional things like count all people who died in retirement homes between march and may were counted as covid deaths (which I find really weird but it seems to work lol). Also, hospitals did struggle (as was the case for many countries) it never got to the point where Belgium relied on expatriating patients to hospitals of neighbouring countries (which was the case for the Netherlands for example) or encouraging 80+ y/o to not go to the hospital is they got sick (which was the case for Sweden), Belgium certainly didn't do good but I doubt it's even in the lowest 25th percentile in Europe let alone the world when it comes to COVID mortality (like seriously they have really good, practically free healthcare). In defense of Belgium: they are very broad in how they define corona-deaths. The Netherlands for example only counts confirmed cases that pass away. Belgium counts confirmed cases, suspected cases and the amount of people that pass away earlier than is to be expected (excess mortality), which by definition also includes deaths not caused by the coronavirus (for example if usually 100 people die in a certain timeframe, and now it's 110. They count those extra 10 as well).

I had to look up the Iceland cannabis thing. It's not true.  "According to that survey which had a response rate of 58.3%, 35.9% of Icelanders 18-67 years old had at some time tried cannabis. Of those who said they had at some time tried cannabis 18.3% said they had smoked weed in the past year. It is this figure the UN, and the Daily Mail are using when they concluded that Icelanders set the world record in weed smoking.  The correct figure would be 6.6%, which is the proportion of Icelanders who had actually smoked weed in the year 2012. This figure puts Iceland in the 29th place in cannabis consumption internationally."

As a Belgian: we have the highest mortality rate because we use adjusted numers, not only the confirmed corona deaths. For instance; the number includes the fact that a certain percentage of people in elderly homes who died, did so due to the virus. So the numbers are adjusted to incorporate the non-confirmed cases too. Debatable weather this is the best way to go about things, because while it might bring us closer to the actual number, it makes comparisons with other countries all the more difficult.
